<user_id>102222591000735908652</user_id><Name>Benjamin Skarcy< /Name><Date>1559930048965<//Date><rating>5< /rating>< review>
This is a great healthy, vegan-friendly (if not totally vegan) juice bar though they have so much more than just juice.  I swung by to pick up a juice and a smoothie for a buddy of mine who ripped his achilles tendon so I was the good samaritan and got him some lunch and decided to get something for myself while I was it.

I choose the peanut butter and banana smoothie which I think the only other ingredient in this smoothie was coconut milk.  It was really refreshing and delicious.  I got a larger size and it kept me full until dinner time.  So good!  It seems like a chain restaurant so I looked them up and they have just a few locations in Southern California which is too bad.  These are the options we need to see more frequently than McDonald's and Jack-in-the-Box.

They have an area that sells snacks, and as if my smoothie wasn't enough, I also bought this peanut butter flavored banana brittle which I also really liked.

It's slightly pricy and the parking is hit or miss since Movita is in a shopping complex with a grocery store and other restaurants and when I came at lunch, it took me awhile to find parking and then had to park on Vons' rooftop just to get some smoothies.

I'll certainly be back but I really hope they do well enough to open up some more locations in and around Los Angeles.<//review>

< review>
The Eagle's Nest is a smaller bar with two pool tables and two dart boards. It's a friendly atmosphere with a good group of regulars. I like to go for Karaoke on any of the five nights they have it. Blue's Night open mic isn't as "open" or inviting as I'd like it to be, but the established performers that are invited to play are talented and nice, though a bit hard of hearing given the volume they crank the speakers up to in such a small room. Overall, it's a nice place to grab a beer or one of a very limited selection of shots and I'll keep going back.<//review>

< Review>
For those who know of this place, you simply can't get enough. For those who never been here, its a laid back bar that provides hundreds of hours of karaoke throughout the week. No matter your mood, you walk away from this play having had a great time and met several people you will definitely run into again. And who knows, you may run into me on a Friday or Saturday rocking the microphone.< /Review>

<name>Jamie A< /name>< review>
When I heard there was a place that did a cupcake and wine pairing, I could not resist. The cupcakes are from Enjoy cupcakes and are $10 and the tasting is $10. I highly recommend your share the cupcakes! They are very rich and even though they are mini-cupcakes, 6 of them is a lot to eat at one time.

The wines are not dessert wines, but it was amazing how well each one paired with the cupcakes. Our server was friendly and did give us a little history about the wines and the Saarloos family. I really enjoyed The Wife. It was described as champagne like without the bubbles, which was a pretty accurate description. The chocolate blackberry Syrah was my favorite cupcake. For a unique experience, be sure and give Saarloos and Sons a try.</review>

<text>I loved this place!  I highly recommend it if you are coming to the Los Olivos/Solvang area.  What makes it super special is that they share space with a cupcake business called Enjoy Cupcakes.  You can buy a $10 cupcake flight (6 mini cupcakes) from Enjoy Cupcakes, then head over to the wine tasting area of Saarloos & Sons for a wine pairing.  I believe the wine tasting at Saarloos was also $10.

The guy who poured our wine was very knowledgeable, friendly and funny.  I actually enjoyed all the wines that were poured.  Maybe it was because of the cupcakes too... really, the wine and cupcake pairing is a must do.

< Review>
WINE&CUPCAKE PAIRING??? YESSS PLEASEEEEE!!!

Thank goodness I stalk my yelp elite friend, Muy S., on facebook! I suggested this place to my sister and she wanted to go as well. This place is located on the busy street of los olives next to Enjoy Cupcake (where they get the cupcakes).

First you buy the cupcakes then walk over to the bar. They'll give you a list of the wines you'll be tasting and you start with the lightest cupcake (in our case it was the honey tangerine).

:: CUPCAKE ::
(6 for $10) you can't choose what you want:
- s'mores stuffed cheescake
- Honey tangerine
- Chocolate blackberry syrah
- Chocolate Pumpkin spice with pecan (loved)
- Vanilla Mango
- Salted Caramel Ginger Snap (my favorite)

:: PROS ::
- CUPCAKES

:: CON ::
- Service wasn't bad but it could have been better, I guess showing up a little before busy hour wasn't enough time for them to be social with us.

:: TIP ::
4 of us shared 1 flight of cupcakes and that was enough to satisfy us.

Overall it was a fun experience. The name of the wines were creative, brotherhood, bride, groom, uncles (?), etc. I wasn't too fond of the wine though :/ most of them went into the bucket.<//Review>

<Name>Francis Chan</Name>< date>
1568003536465<//date>
< rating>
5<//rating>
<review>I met with Kevin on my first appointment and hee hawed around. I've been surfing a lot on my 5'10" quad but wanted something that would have more volume, not a quad setup, and I had been looking at speed eggs but also had some interest in a groveler (a bit opposite...).

Kevin was super patient but when he showed me the Easy Button speed eggs, I knew I was sold on the shape. I had been looking at the FCD HR but those things are hard to find and in the right volume I wanted. I left without a board but then when I got home set another appointment to drive back up the next day.

I met Jon the next morning and it came down to a 6'6" or 7' EB Speed Egg. For the price, I settled with the 6'6". It had the right volume, the deck patches for more durability, and the shape that I wanted. Took it out Del Mar in 4-5ft chop and their recommendation did not disappoint! First ride was a nice right with a sweeping bottom turn to the lip then a nice cruise to finish. Smooth!

I was actually able to duck dive the board (roughly 43L @ 170# 6') but if I mistimed it definitely is not as forgiving as a my quad.

I'm glad I found this place. No BS, just boards, boards, boards. My next one is coming from this place for sure. The appointment system was painless and really enjoyable to have time 1:1 with the owners to talk things over. <review>MTP - As of 3/28- awesome place to shop vintage and high and low brow wares. Must wear a mask to enter and pay for a ticket. Proceeds benefit art programs for the fairfax highschool grounds that the market takes place on. Some vendors will also negotiate the prices. I bought a vintage italian sweater from the 70s for $25 instead of 35. And a Canon 35 mm camera from ' 99 for $60.
Not bad!
They also have many garden and house plants as well as holistic and organic options to clean your home.
But if you're looking for cheap costume jewelry, sun glasses and the perfect distressed tee, this ... Is the spot to be.< /review>< rate>

< review>
The place to find unique one-off items. From clothing and accessories to furniture and trinkets. I love wandering around the aisles, getting lost and promising myself not to spend any more money. Hard to do.

They raised entrance fee prices from $3 to $5. Cash is best to have on you for most of these merchants.

Come right when it opens to find the best items. Or if you just want to browse, take your time and get here before they close or else you‚Äôll get a million reminders on the loud speaker about closing in x-amount of minutes.

There‚Äôs a cute food court area - all located out doors. Get coffees here, rest your legs and unwind.

I love how people who shop here are wearing amazing, trendy clothes.< /review>

Awesome market. only a cupla bucks to enter main gate.Anything and everything type traders. We found treasures! New hand painted shirts through to vintage glass! Held at Fairfax High School grounds on Melrose, only on Sunday, the area this market takes up was very worthwhile taking the time to go and wander through, as it‚Äôs extensive. <Rating>4< /Rating>< review>
This is the place to go to in downtown when you don't know exactly what you want to eat or when you're with a lot of people and you can't decide where to eat. This place is packed with flavor from different parts of the world. I was able to see Thai food, Chinese food, Salvadorian food, Mexican food, Italian food, and even vegan food (yes, I know vegan food isn't a part of the world but it deserves recognition as a food category haha). There are also little markets inside that sell produce, meat, spices, and candies. This place has it all!<//review>

<Rating>5<//Rating>< review>
I could go on and on about this flea market - I have devotedly attended this Sunday tradition for years now and have watched it steadily grow in size, vendors, and popularity.  You can find an eclectic variety of wares here: vintage clothing, artisan and vintage jewelry, houseplants, antiques, local artists, new furniture from local craftsmen, food for all tastes and diets, knick-knacks galore, and even more items in between. Most vendors inside accept cash and cards, but be prepared for the cash-only entrance fee of $5. You‚Äôre guaranteed to find something you didn‚Äôt know you wanted every time you go.< /review>

< review>
This is a relatively fun, but small flea. It carries a $5 entry, but once you're in you're greeted with mostly vintage clothes, a few succulents and/or house plants vendors, some vintage print places, local Jewelers, vintage furniture, and a pretty great coffee place. It's more of a quirky outdoor home decor shop with a cover fee, but it does have its gems. Go here for clothing, or home decor. Don't come here for bargain hunting and lots of treasure hunting.< /review>

< text>
Non-profit partnership between Greenway Arts Alliance and Fairfax High School to bring a flourishing community market, professional theatre and arts education/life programming to the Melrose & Fairfax neighborhood.
Awesome local & independent businesses, artists, musicians, designers, collectors and makers fill the market every Sunday.
Your $3 admission fee directly benefits students at Fairfax High.
Art & local commerce uplifting the community = everyone wins< /text>

<Text>If you check the website, there's usually a coupon for $1 off entry.

Early bird def gets the worm here.  If you arrive early there's parking, but if you are like most of LA you aren't gonna get any parking, good luck with that!

< Review>
Its a street market showcasing local artistry and people's vintage finds. What other would call junk could also be another person's treasure. No shortage of old clothes and ornaments. There's a vendor there that has a whole department store section for aloha shirts for 7.00. Great fit for summer or for a gift for your trendy teen. It's bigger than you think so take the time to explore. Also, say hi to all the dogs you'll see. Came around 1:20, didn't find parking until 2:00 so I suggest coming early. There's also a mini street market across the street. It's a great Instagram photo spot due to the fact that there's an angel wing mural at the entrance of it. Great place to visit for 2 or so hours.<//Review>

Entry fee is under $5 and you can literally spend a whole day here checking out the shops, some live music and a delicious snow cone.
